    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_314987236" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/314987236" />
    <a title="Tara Calaby" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1097242-tara-calaby"><img alt="Tara Calaby" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1563888338p2/1097242.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/314987236?book_show_action=true">Apr 18, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tara Calaby" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tara Calaby" href="/user/show/1097242-tara-calaby">Tara Calaby</a>
      </span>

          added it


          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781447206804" href="/book/show/13496376-fated">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1097242-tara-calaby?shelf=used-to-own">used-to-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1097242-tara-calaby?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1097242-tara-calaby?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1097242-tara-calaby?shelf=review-copy">review-copy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer314987236" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13633121398751846686"><b>The Cover:</b> <br/>It's gorgeous. I love the yellow background, which is quite unusual, and the sepia toning used for the photo of Daire. The way her hair evolves into the flock of ravens is graphically attractive and a great hint at the novel's content. I'm loving the font, as well. <br/><br/><b>The Protagonist:</b> <br/>I liked Daire, even if I have no idea how to pronounce her name. (Then again, this is the same for <i>most</i> of the characters in <i>Fated</i>. What is it about paranormal YA and names I've never heard of?) I think tha</span>
  <span id="freeText13633121398751846686" style="display:none"><b>The Cover:</b> <br />It's gorgeous. I love the yellow background, which is quite unusual, and the sepia toning used for the photo of Daire. The way her hair evolves into the flock of ravens is graphically attractive and a great hint at the novel's content. I'm loving the font, as well. <br /><br /><b>The Protagonist:</b> <br />I liked Daire, even if I have no idea how to pronounce her name. (Then again, this is the same for <i>most</i> of the characters in <i>Fated</i>. What is it about paranormal YA and names I've never heard of?) I think that Noël did a good job of giving reason for Daire's independence and flexibility. Most teenagers would be completely thrown by the revelations that Daire has to quickly take on board, but her background travelling the world means that she is used to change and instability. I also appreciate the fact that Daire is the character whose powers form the focus of <i>Fated</i>. So often with paranormal romance, it's all about the boy being special, and it's always nice to have a protagonist who is powerful in her own right.<br /><br /><b>The Antagonist:</b> <br />I get the impression that we'll be seeing a lot more of Cade in further novels. In <i>Fated</i>, he's a little two dimensional. We know he's dangerous, because everyone tells Daire that he is, but we don't really see much of his power. I did, however, appreciate that there was no hint of a love triangle involving Cade and his twin, Dace – at least from Daire's point of view. <br /><br /><b>The Love Interest:</b> <br /><i>Fated</i> falls into the instalove category of paranormals, unfortunately. Daire and Dace's attraction is fated before they even meet, and so there is no slow build-up to romance in the novel, or even to friendship. Dace himself is a likeable character, however, and I think he'll be a big hit with young readers. There's a slight Jacob Black feel to him, with his Native American heritage and long black hair, which I'm sure will go down well! I appreciate the fact that he's nothing but kind to Daire and her loved ones – no creepy YA boyfriend syndrome here. In this first novel, his and Daire's connection is largely physical, which meant that I found it a little wanting in the depth department. I did, however, appreciate the fact that there was no moral judgement attached to Daire's sexual urges. <br /><br /><b>The Supporting Cast:</b> <br />I enjoyed Paloma, but my favourite minor character was definitely Chay. I'd love to see more discussion of their relationship in future novels. Xotichl was likeable, although I don't understand including a character name that you <i>know</i> people won't be able to pronounce, and I was intrigued by Lita. I think Jennika, Daire's mother, would have bothered me more if I didn't know her backstory and a little about the place she comes from with her decisions, but as it was, I actually thought she was a well-crafted character. <br /><br /><b>The Plot:</b> <br /><i>Fated</i> is the first book in a series, which means that there is a <i>lot</i> of setting up to be found in the first couple of hundred pages. I've read other reviews from people who haven't been able to make it past this section of the book to the action, and I can understand why. It felt like there was an awful lot of waiting around before things actually started to happen. That said, Noël has come up with an interesting concept, and it will be interesting to see where she goes with it. By the end of the novel, the reader is still left with a lot of questions about what Daire is and how she will have to use her new-found powers. When it comes to a series, I think it's generally unfair to judge the first book <i>too</i> harshly for having a slow start, because all of that exposition has to happen <i>somewhere</i>. I did find myself wishing, however, that there had been a little more of a pay off for the long introduction when the meat of the story finally began. <br /><br /><b>The Writing:</b> <br />Noël's writing style was actually the thing I struggled most with while reading <i>Fated</i>. She uses sentence fragments. A <i>lot</i> of fragments. Building on previous sentences. Adding information. Rarely using grammar as it was intended. <br /><br />See what I did there? Look, I'm a big fan of learning the rules of grammar and then <i>using</i> this knowledge to break the rules here and there in order to add interest to your writing. I think there comes a point, though, where this kind of thing can become distracting and, with <i>Fated</i>, I was constantly pulled out of the story by the lack of proper sentence structure. I enjoy an occasional sentence fragment, and use them for pacing and emphasis myself. When it reaches the point, however, where a half-page paragraph consists of one initial sentence followed solely by fragments, it just doesn't work for me. Others may well consider it stylistically brilliant. <br /><br /><b>The Verdict:</b> <br /><i>Fated</i> is sure to find its place in the current YA paranormal market. I think there's still a large demand for this kind of story and, while there is nothing very <i>new</i> about <i>Fated</i>, it is this that is likely to ensure it becomes a hit with its intended demographic. I personally struggled with Noël's writing style and a plot that failed to ignite a spark of excitement in me, but I believe that <i>Fated</i> will do well and will amass many fans – not <i>all</i> of whom will be in it solely for Dace!<br /><br /><b>(1.5 stars)</b><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13633121398751846686" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_337812577" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/337812577" />
    <a title="Emily" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9622944-emily"><img alt="Emily" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1339296966p2/9622944.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/337812577?book_show_action=true">May 27, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily" href="/user/show/9622944-emily">Emily</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781466802544" href="/book/show/13167705-fated">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer337812577" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7922670283706848734"><b>The Good</b><br/>- The Cover<br/>Seriously, how awesome is that cover? There’s badass birds and cool chic earrings with a really creepy font and ominous title. It pretty much hits every ticky box on the YA cover checklist.<br/><br/>- Secondary Characters<br/>I would sometimes find myself more intrigued with the secondary characters’ back story than I was with any of the actual current plot they are involved with. Which probably does not speak highly of the actual plot, but kudos to the author for creating a rather diverse c</span>
  <span id="freeText7922670283706848734" style="display:none"><b>The Good</b><br />- The Cover<br />Seriously, how awesome is that cover? There’s badass birds and cool chic earrings with a really creepy font and ominous title. It pretty much hits every ticky box on the YA cover checklist.<br /><br />- Secondary Characters<br />I would sometimes find myself more intrigued with the secondary characters’ back story than I was with any of the actual current plot they are involved with. Which probably does not speak highly of the actual plot, but kudos to the author for creating a rather diverse cast of characters -- some of them very intriguing.<br /><br />- The Premise<br />You had me at “glowing people stalk her and time stops without warning”. Seriously, it does not take much to get me interested. As a reader, I’m just looking for a little escapism and this sounds like something I can dive right into. I enjoyed much of the worldbuilding when the book actually got around to it. Those few intriguing morsels are pretty much all that kept me from abandoning this when the plot started to grind to a halt.<br /><br /><br /><b>The Bad</b><br />- The Length and Pace<br />This is a seriously long book (or maybe it just felt that way?) and much of the writing is so clunky and flowery that I feel the length could have been cut down a lot and the plot could have been tightened just by cutting ⅓ of the unnecessarily dense language. Reading this book is a serious test of endurance.<br /><br />- The Plot<br />There is a lot of back story to get to and it sometimes feels like the plot takes a backseat to rather frequent sessions of info dumping. The writing is so verbose that I actually skimmed a lot and I’m pretty sure I didn’t miss much. Halfway into the story the main action and mystery is still being set up so it’s a lot of slow going at first. Hopefully the other three books can move along to the main point faster since a lot of the groundwork has already been set up, but I doubt I’ll be picking up the second book to see.<br /><br />- Characters<br />It’s probably a bad sign that I found the Mean Girl and the Bad Guy to be some of the most interesting characters in this story. The main character, Daire, has a serious case of Attitude and that doesn’t change until at least halfway into the book. I love rebellious loners, but in this case Daire just seems like a Brat. She and her mother are supposed to be super close, but Daire seems to have little respect for that bond.<br /><br />- The Names<br />While the names of important characters should probably be unique and memorable, the author seems to take this to the extreme. For example, the brothers have very unique but similar names. Not helpful when I’m trying to keep them apart and swallowing so much info.<br /><br />- InstaLove<br />Daire dreams about her One True Love before they’ve even met. So when they do meet, there is pretty much no question that they will get together even though it doesn’t technically happen until very far into the story. What we do see of their relationship is a lot of getting physical pretty fast.<br /><br /><b>The Verdict</b><br />I would recommend this to readers who are already fans of Noel’s verbose writing style and avid readers of paranormal who are willing to slog through a lot of setup to get to the main action.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7922670283706848734" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('1KzFs8gLrN17N/vejhmDc9OvRs/uE5bBubxD2LDEr5hSw8JH4fuc43wR4ELb0hMhnc8ABGwGfQ2fEjN2SacOwQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('okqfldK8IgJXzgUXvAvRiw3BvTMIjZSt8pkTVFUT8QQkJZhh+0wSPFDoHovpwEHZQ6H7+IqYf2HUN2P6rHBQXQ==')})
  }
